I spent my Christmas Eve 12/24/2019, Christmas Day 12/25/2019 and discharged on 12/26/2019 at Hazel Hawkins Memorial Hospital. My husband and I was just visiting family for the holidays and to our surprise, I was admitted to the ER in the morning of Christmas Eve due to severe pain  that was unmanageable, then sent to emergency surgery shortly after assessment due to my medical illness advancing.

The staff was so pleasant and understanding from admission in the ER, Admission Nurse, ER doctor to OB-GYN Surgeon till the day I was discharged.

THANK YOU TO ALL the Staff that helped me!

I'm so glad I was able to write down  some of the names that helped me during my stay. If I do not mention your name, it's because I wasn't all there in my head, but you are great and you loved by the McDonald Family!

Benito,  Eddie and Ismael

POST OPERATION TEAM- Thank you!

Christmas EVE night (focused on pain management) 1st night

Day after Christmas 12/26/2019 -discharge day

I went to Hazel Hawkins for an ultrasound because my baby was in a weird position and my midwife wanted to get the exact position figured out.  She recommended seeing someone in San Jose but I didn't want to drive that far just for an ultrasound, so I went to Hazel Hawkins because I live within 2 miles of the hospital.  My mistake! <Rating>4</Rating><Text>This is a great school with a variety of classes available to the public. If you are looking to get your G.E.D or finish your high school diploma, this is the place. It also offers ESL classes which are unfortunately impacted but there is a waitlist for those who are interested. You will be given a brief English test, assessed and then placed on the list. This place is also a CSET testing site. Parking is limited due to the large number of students in attendance. The formal parking lot has security and a supervised bike lock up area. If you are taking the metro, El Monte Busway is just a 10 minute walk down the street. Bus 76 and 268 pass directly in front of the school on their way to and from the depot. There are also some Foothill buses that run past as well. The area is relatively active at night with people frequenting businesses or attending the school.< /Text>< pictures>

< Text>
I have been a happy patient of Dr. Bickman's for a decade. She is a kind, warm, caring, empathetic doctor, with a wonderful bedside manner. As doctors go, you cannot do better. I have lost track of how many people I've referred to her over the years. So it pains me to write this, but I would not want anyone else to go through what I am currently going through. After a decade of conversations about her kids and my kids and yoga and everything else under the sun, I went to see Dr. Bickman for my annual exam October 20th. I checked the box for new insurance and gave the front desk my new card, which they copied and gave back to me. Dr. Bickman was running behind that day, so after an hour I let the front desk know I was leaving and would call to reschedule. When I called, I was again asked over the phone if my insurance had changed since my last visit, and I said that it had, and that the office had made a copy of my new card when I was there. The woman on the phone (whom I assume was Grace) said she could see that in my chart. I came in on October 28th for my rescheduled appointment and again checked the box for new insurance and again confirmed they had my new information, which they said they did. Had my exam, and was then hit with a bill for $5715 because it turns out Dr. Bickman does not accept my new insurance, she is out-of-network and all claims were denied as a result. My insurance company has no record of anyone from Dr. Bickman's office or billing department calling to check eligibility, which is standard practice. Grace told me easily and kindly on the phone that this was "definitely their mistake" nonetheless no one has helped me get this resolved. I have now spent months during a pandemic when we all have too much on our plates already, making phone calls and sending emails trying to get the office to make this right. Grace also acknowledged her understanding that I would not have come in if I'd known Dr. Bickman was out-of-network. Finally, when I couldn't get anywhere with the front desk or billing, I asked for Dr. Bickman's email, feeling certain she did not know what was happening. Not sure what my next steps are, but since no one at the office seems to be ready to do the right thing, perhaps a public testimonial will get me the help I need. I own a business, and I must say this is not the way you treat anyone, let alone a loyal patient of a decade! So utterly disappointed.</Text>

< text>
It's taken me three years to even be able to speak about my experience with Dr. Bickman without balling my eyes out. A friend finally insisted I write a review in hopes it would help avoid any trauma for whomever may be reading this.

I'll start by saying that I prepared for birth by practicing hypo birthing during my pregnancy. I was upfront about what I wanted with Dr. Bickman and presented my birthing plan. She seemed on board the entire time during my pregnancy. I told her I would have a doula present and that my wish was to have a natural birth, and not induce as long as everyone was healthy.

Well, everything went fine. My birthing time at the hospital was fine. The nurses at St. Johns were awesome. I labored for 30 hrs before being induced, which was not my plan but it was also my choice in the moment. I was so exhausted and I wasn't progressing.

But when it came time to push, I pushed for three hours.  It was a Friday, and I imagine Dr. Bickman had a room full of patients at her office. I was probably two hours into pushing and the head started to show, so the nurses phoned the doctor. I felt ready to really push and the nurses told me to wait until the doctor showed up, "15 minutes" they said. I begged they just get any doctor in, but was told to wait.

When she finally came in (not 15 min),  the whole energy in the room shifted. She came in rushed, constantly looking at her phone. Whatever progress I had made, wasn't there anymore. The head wasn't showing anymore. The nurses demeanor changed. At one point doctor Bickman yelled at the nurse, "I thought you said the head was almost out", and THREW her gloves at her, "These are the wrong ones". The energy went from peaceful to tense in less than 10 seconds. The nurses kept telling me to push and the doctor was just on her phone looking impatience. It took all I had to close my eyes, go to my happy place (thank goodness for hypnosis and my doula), and push my baby out.

The worst is what happened after. The epidural had worn off. I had a natural tear from birthing. Suddenly the doctor was shoving her hands all over without any explanation. There was no, " okay, you tore and we are going to stitch", or "I'm now going to shove something up you butt to help with the pain". I had my baby on my chest and her hands were shoving and pinching. I felt every stitch. I was in such pain that I broke that things that hold your legs up and the nurses had to hold my legs. My body went into shock after. At first I assumed that perhaps, it was an emergency and I was bleeding to death. But after speaking to my doula, she said she had never witnesses such rudeness, or violent handling.

She never had the best bedside manners, and perhaps that should have been a red flag for me. Needless to say, I switched my doctor and did not go back to her postpartum. I feel like she robbed me of that moment that we as becoming mothers, dream about: when you first meet your baby on your chest. If she had explained to me what was going on, so that I could expect it maybe I wouldn't feel so violated. But her attitude towards the nurses, her disregard of me, rudeness and lack of bedside manners left a traumatizing mark on my birthing experience that I still have trouble talking about.

Look, no matter what your birthing plan is, things will happen they way your baby chooses and change last minute. BUT you still have the right to have compassionate caregivers at your side, no matter what. If you are envisioning a more natural, peaceful birth for yourself, this is not your doctor.</text>

<user_id>105717678786744653604< /user_id>< text>
Dr. Bickman is by far the best OBGYN I have ever had. I moved to LA three years ago and was referred to Dr. Bickman from my primary care physician. I needed a Dr. in the UCLA health system that was located close enough to my office in Santa Monica so that I could have appointments before/during work. Three years and two children later I would highly recommend Dr. Bickman to ANYONE.

I never had to wait longer than 30 minutes for an appointment. If I ever suspected that she was running behind schedule (due to a delivery or patient emergency) I would just call the office and ask so they could give me an idea of what time to come in. She is flexible and has even allowed me to make last minute appointments as well.

I love her bedside manner. I like to ask a lot of questions and am curious about EVERYTHING. Dr. Bickman has always taken time to talk to me about my concerns and share her knowledge. She is obviously very busy and wants to make sure everyone gets the same level of attention. You can tell by the way she runs around her office going from room to room, patient to patient that she doesn't like to keep people waiting, yet I never felt rushed or neglected.

Both of my pregnancies were high risk and Dr. Bickman handled each with diligent care and concern. I had to be hospitalized for two months during my first pregnancy and she visited me (along with any other patients she had on bedrest) EVERY DAY in the hospital, even on her days off. For both of my pregnancies she referred me to a perinatologist to help manage my pregnancy. I was impressed that she continued to lead my case and work closely with him to manage any procedures or make any decisions regarding my health and the health of the baby. She was involved every step of the way and delivered both of my children! Its clear she invests in her patients and takes time to understand her patients history and condition. She doesn't make you feel bad or uncomfortable about anything and can relate to almost EVERYTHING we go through because she is a woman with children herself.< /text>

<user>115306109642556829939< /user><user_name>Christine Orth< /user_name><Date>1461621153006</Date><rate>5<//rate>< Text>
This little dealership in Nipomo should not be overlooked if you are in the market for a used car! There are many things I liked about it. One, the inventory is not overwhelming. Sometimes if there are hundreds of cars, it's just too much. Also, cars are very clean and in good shape. There's a nice variety from SUV's to sedans to more sporty options. However, what impressed me most was the owner/manager Matt. He was so helpful and so friendly, but never pushy. And he was happy to pull up the car faxes for the cars we were interested in. Car shopping, which can often be quite stressful, was a pleasant experience here!< /Text>

<Name>Ginger Elliott<//Name>< Review>
This may be an odd review considering the final purchase wasn't with Auto Source, but I don't want to pass up the opportunity to praise a recent experience there with Matthew. A family member was looking to buy a car and based on a listing she saw for one she was interested in, we drove up to Nipomo to check it out. As others here have mentioned, it's a tiny showroom that you wouldn't easily notice from the road, but they had several nice vehicles of different categories and at varying price points. Also as mentioned, there was no pressure. Dealing with Matthew was so pleasant. He stayed far past closing to help us, kindly offered a lot of other information and guidance not tied to "making a sale" that I believe will be invaluable in the long run, and was generous with his time and communication over the couple of days that he worked with us. He was completely amenable to our taking the car to a mechanic of our choosing for a pre-purchase inspection (something I'd strongly recommend to anyone no matter who you're buying from and especially if buying from a business where they're not specializing in one type of car and don't have their own service department). As we didn't live nearby, Matthew had the car transported to the mechanic we chose so that I wouldn't have to leave work early in order to get it there. It turned out there was an issue with the vehicle that had been missed (can happen and we later discovered from someone else why it may have gotten missed, but I appreciated the transparency we encountered). Rather than trying to "make it work" with that car, the final purchase ended up being another vehicle found elsewhere, but I wish things had worked out so that the sale could have been given to Matthew at Auto Source. When my husband and I are in need of another vehicle, I'd happily start looking there.< /Review>

<userid>102075195216525523515</userid><Response>None<//Response>< Name>
Sean Schluntz<//Name>
<Gmap_id>0x808e5564f785b16b:0x6778d74ee78c4781</Gmap_id>< Review>
This is an interesting place, it's setup like a fancy / high end restaurant and charges the prices you would expect for one but is also accepting of the people who are camping in the RV or Tent sites. It's nice that it's open like that.

They start you off with a nice bagett / sourdough loaf and garlic butter  I had Cesar salad and Cioppino and my wife the clam chowder, corn risotto and crab cakes.

The salad was good but in one of those strange fancy / not moments I wasn't offered ground pepper with it - I made due with the pepper on the table. The Cioppino had a flavorful but watery broth with a fair helping of seafood but it was all a bit overcooked (tough shrimp, fish that would have been dry if not in broth). I wasn't dissapointed, it wasn't bad, it was just average.

My wife reported the chowder was also on the thin side but had good flavor and she really enjoyed the crab cakes and risotto.

The restaurant has a full bad and I found the local speciality generous in size and surprisingly inexpensive as far as mixed drinks go.

I've been here before and have never had a bad meal (they have mad good cobblers in the past) and if you are already here it's a nice place to eat. I don't think I would make it a destination. Though, ~25 miles up the coast are quite a few other options, probably the same south of here.<//Review>

I took my boyfriend here for Valentines Day a two years ago. The setting was nice, and I recall the food being decent. <name>Bill Hogarth</name><Time>1558373136412</Time><rating>5< /rating>< Review>
Breakfast on Sunday, coming over the hill from Coalinga to get to the 101. We love finding good locally-owned restaurants, trying new foods and were intrigued by this place. We were not disappointed. It was busy but not crowded with the building worn but clean. The staff was quick and courteous. I ordered the Sinaloan breakfast (spicy egg scramble with peppers, beans, and a rice medley). It was delicious with a slightly vinegary spicy flavor to the eggs, but the beans were to die for. The we're white beans and partly mashed similar to refried but not. My wife chose the chorizo and egg breakfast and she too loved the meal (although she said the chorizo was a little too oily, I noticed she ate it all). All ingredients we're fresh and we'll seasoned altho the rice medley may have used some prepared corn and carrots. Oh, and the chips came with one of the best table salsas I've ever had. The price was fair, but not cheap. I will probably never be traveling thru there again, but if I do this is a must-stop.<//Review>

< Text>
I urge anyone to take a trip to Sunland Produce Market. The prices on Vegetables and fruits are unbeatable. The ethnic food of every part of the world is in the aisles. The meat section is plenty and they have just about any type of cut and meat in stock.

Pictured are Pasilla peppers that will be made into Chili Rellenos.

Every part of the world seems to be represented there.

I highly recommend Sunland Produce Market for any of your fruit and vegetable needs.< /Text>

<user_name>Joan Lowell< /user_name><Rating>5</Rating></record></dataset><record>
< gmap_id>
0x80c2946dba1acc81:0x4c81184b6e38e1a7< /gmap_id>
< Rate>
4</Rate>
<Resp>None</Resp>< review>
Big, clean space, not particularly aesthetically pleasing. That is not the point. For the most part, its main draw is the bargains you can find here, e.g. 5 lbs of dates for $10, Bulgarian feta cheese for $2.98, big Panettone cake for $5, etc.

Vast area reserved for vegetables & fruits much of it discounted. (Don't buy too much since they may spoil earlier because they may be older hence the possible discount). Huge spice & herb selection. Dried fruits, nuts, seeds. Large display of  cheese, meat & processed meats such as sausages, Bologna not necessarily made in Italy but somewhere in Eastern Europe.

Much of the processed foods veer between Latin American & Armenian. But with Armenians spread out over Iran, Lebanon, Syria as well as having been part of the former USSR, there is good representation of Middle Eastern & Eastern European.

Nice presentation of food from far corners of the world. Good way to stretch your dollar if you know the prevailing undiscounted price of the food items you are buying in order to comparison shop.<//review>

<rate>4</rate><Review>A mid-sized Supermarket with an unrivaled selection of fruits & vegetables but, also with 'not-so-super' service.

Located near the Gateway to Shadow Hills, at the intersection of Sunland and Glenoaks Blvds. this single location operation has offered the East valley an outstanding selection of fresh produce since 1990. Following the closure of Ralphs last year it is now the ONLY grocery store within a three mile radius, a situation which has certainly increased sales volume...unfortunately at the expense of prompt service. I would recommend avoiding weekend visits, unless you enjoy full parking lots and long lines!

The store offers a full  Meat Counter with reasonably priced weekly specials, for example: ground beef @ $1.79 lb or T-bone steak @ $4.99 lb. The service at this counter is usually prompt and the sale items are generally in stock. My only complaint is that (like most local markets) they don't seem to employ a trained butcher, instead their "meat cutters" slice everything except the roasts almost paper thin.

A "full service" deli counter offers a good variety of meats and cheeses, but delivers them in an almost comically lackadaisical manner. For example; while holding a "take-a-number" which had at least nine people ahead of me in line, I watched as three employees engaged in a 5 minute debate about who was gonna sweep the floor...which was only resolved after a fourth employee joined. THEN, all four went in different directions to search for the dust-mop, without so much as a glance toward the 11 or 12 unfortunate souls who just wanted some Swiss Cheeze!

The general merchandise is heavy with eastern European offerings as is their dairy selection. The store is not the cleanest that I've ever been in, but not filthy either. Beware, they close very early at seven (7 PM) so don't go looking for a late-night snack!

Oh yeah. One last little complaint: This is the ONLY store I have ever been two which charges an additional dollar for Marlborough 100 cigarettes (above the price for Marlborough Red kings)! So if Marl. Reds were $5.49 a pack, then Marl 100 Reds would be $6.49 per pack, the problem is that they both have the exact same amount of tobacco per cig. AND they both cost the same to buy wholesale.

Despite my tepid review, I must admit that I do shop here at least once a week - the produce selection is That Good!<//Review>< gmap_id>
